    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6044209778521145669">In this startling historical mystery, unique in the author's canon, Agatha Christie presents the puzzle of a deadly mystery at the heart of a dissonant family in ancient Egypt. Imhotep, wealthy landowner and priest of Thebes, has outraged his sons and daughters by bringing a beautiful concubine into their fold. And the manipulative Nofret has already set about a plan to us</span>
  <span id="freeText6044209778521145669" style="display:none">In this startling historical mystery, unique in the author's canon, Agatha Christie presents the puzzle of a deadly mystery at the heart of a dissonant family in ancient Egypt. Imhotep, wealthy landowner and priest of Thebes, has outraged his sons and daughters by bringing a beautiful concubine into their fold. And the manipulative Nofret has already set about a plan to usurp her rivals' rightful legacies. When her lifeless body is discovered at the foot of a cliff, Imhotep's own flesh and blood become the apparent conspirators in her shocking murder. But vengeance and greed may not be the only motives...</span>
  <a data-text-id="6044209778521145669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16640073624785649104">Death comes as the End, Agatha Christie<br/><br/>Death Comes as the End is a historical mystery novel by Agatha Christie, first published in October 1944. <br/><br/>The suggestion to base the story in ancient Egypt came from noted Egyptologist and family friend Stephen Glanville. <br/><br/>He also assisted Christie with details of daily household life in Egypt 4000 years ago.   <span id="freeText16640073624785649104" style="display:none">Death comes as the End, Agatha Christie<br /><br />Death Comes as the End is a historical mystery novel by Agatha Christie, first published in October 1944. <br /><br />The suggestion to base the story in ancient Egypt came from noted Egyptologist and family friend Stephen Glanville. <br /><br />He also assisted Christie with details of daily household life in Egypt 4000 years ago. A young widow reacquainting herself with her family when her father Imhotep, a successful but pompous and short-sighted mortuary priest, brings a new "wife", Nofret, into their lives. <br /><br />Nofret soon disrupts and antagonises Imhotep's sons - Yahmose, Sobek and Ipy - as well as their wives. Renisenb realises the housekeeper Henet, while feigning devotion, is full of hatred. She eventually confronts Henet, who in a fit of pique admits she hates Renisenb and hated Renisenb's long-deceased mother. ...<br /><br />عنوانهای: «فرجام»؛ «مرگ فرجام کار است»، «مرگ، نقطه ی پایان»، «مرگ، چون پایانی فرا میرسد»، «مرگ نقطه پایان»؛ «و سرانجام مرگ»؛ نویسنده: آگ‍ات‍ا ک‍ری‍س‍ت‍ی‌؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش دوم: در سال 2005 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: م‍رگ‌، ن‍ق‍طه ‌ی‌ پ‍ای‍ان‌؛ نویسنده: آگ‍ات‍ا ک‍ری‍س‍ت‍ی‌؛ ب‍رگ‍ردان‌: ای‍ل‍ی‍ا ح‍ری‍ری‌؛ ت‍ه‍ران: ک‍اروان‌‏‫، 1381؛ در 312ص؛ شابک 9647033362؛ چاپ دوم 1382؛ چاپ چهارم 1385؛ چاپ پنجم 1386؛ چاپ ششم 1387؛ شابک 9789647033367؛ چاپ دیگر تهران‏‫ نشر قطره‏‫، 1389؛ در 320ص؛ شابک 9786001191978؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان بریتانیایی - سده 20م<br /><br />این اثر با عنوانهای: «فرجام»؛ «مرگ فرجام کار است»، «مرگ، نقطه ی پایان»، «مرگ، چون پایانی فرا میرسد»، «مرگ نقطه پایان»؛ «و سرانجام مرگ»؛ در سالهای گوناگون چاپ شده است<br /><br />نقل نمونه متن کتاب: «نگاهش از روی دره در آن پایین، رو به خط نقره ای نیل کشید و فراتر رفت» پایان نقل از متن کتاب<br /><br />بر کرجی‌ مرگ «رونی سنب» و «خای» در جهان‌ زیرین شناور بودند؛ همچنان‌که به سپیده‌ دم نزدیک می‌شدند، «خای» سرش را برگرداند، و «رنی سنب» دید که او «خای» نیست و «کامنی» است؛ و در همان زمان دماغه‌ ی قایق که به شکل سر مار بود، آغاز کرد به پیچ و تاب خوردن، دماغه مار زنده بود، یک کبرا؛ «رنی سنب» فکر کرد که این همان ماری است که از آرامگاه بیرون می‌آید، تا ارواح مردگان را ببلعد؛ بعد دید که سر مار به شکل چهره‌ ی «نوفرت» است، و فریاد زنان از خواب پرید<br /><br />نقل از آغاز متن: «یک: دومین ماه فصل طغیان-روز بیستم؛ «رِنی سِنْب»، خیره به نیل ایستاده بود؛ میتوانست از دور صدای بلند برادرانش «یاحموز» و «سوبِک» را، بشنود؛ داشتند بحث میکردند که آیا لازم است آب بندی، در جایی مخصوص تقویت بشود یا خیر؛ صدای «سوبک»، مثل همیشه، بلند و مطمئن بود؛ عادت داشت نظرش را با جدیت ملایمی به کرسی بنشاند؛ صدای «یاحموز» ملایم و لرزان بود، و تردید و اضطراب او را میرساند؛ همیشه درباره ی چیزی مضطرب بود؛ بزرگترین پسر بود و در غیاب پدرش، زمانی که به اراضی شمالی میرفت، سرپرستی مزارع کم و بیش به عهده ی او بود؛ کند و محتاط، و نگران مشکلاتی بود که وجود نداشتند؛ مرد درشت اندام لَختی بود، که از سبکبالی و اعتماد به نفسِ «سوبک» بهره ای نبرده بود؛ «رنی سنب» به یاد میآورد که از اوان کودکی، جر و بحث برادران بزرگترش را، با شیوه ی مخصوص هرکدام شنیده است؛ ناگهان این موضوع احساس امنیتی به او بخشید...؛ دوباره در خانه بود؛ بله، به خانه باز گشته بود...؛ اما وقتی به آنسوی رود روشن و درخشان نگریست، طغیان و درد درونی اش دوباره بیدار شد؛ «خای»، شوهر جوانش، مرده بود...؛ «خای»، با آن چهره ی خندان و شانه های نیرومند؛ «خای» با «اوزیریس» در قلمرو مردگان بود و او، «رنی سنب»، همسر دلبندش، وانهاده شده بود؛ هشت سال با هم گذرانده بودند - زمانی که با شوهرش ازدواج کرد، تنها کمی از یک کودک بزرگتر بود- و اکنون بیوه شده، با دختر «خای»، «تِتی»، به خانه ی پدری اش باز گشته بود<br /><br />در این لحظه به نظرش میرسید که هرگز این خانه را ترک نکرده بوده است...؛ به پیشواز این اندیشه رفت...؛ آن هشت سال را فراموش میکرد -هشت سال سرشار از شادی تصور نشدنی، که آنچنان با درد و جدایی پاره پاره و نابود شده بود؛ بله، فراموش میکرد، از اندیشه بیرونش میکرد؛ دوباره «رنی سنب» میشد، بار دیگر به دختر «ایمحوتِپ»، «کاهن کا» تبدیل میشد.». پایان نقل<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 13/04/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1814807335?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bren" href="/user/show/61659069-bren">Bren</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814807335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8463948796048346036">“A trifle, a little, the likeness of a dream. And death comes as the end.” <br/>― Agatha Christie, Death Comes as the End<br/><br/>EDIT..8/8/2020<br/>Revisited during storm. Still adore it. First read when I was like eight or nine. <br/><br/>Gave it to my dad during the storm when I was done. He'd never read it. He finished it in a night and LOVED it. And no, did not guess the culprit.<br/><br/>My review:<br/><br/>Why is does this book not have a solid 5 star average rating? Oh no..my bias is showing.<br/><br/>I first read this book as a child, after see</span>
  <span id="freeText8463948796048346036" style="display:none">“A trifle, a little, the likeness of a dream. And death comes as the end.” <br />― Agatha Christie, Death Comes as the End<br /><br />EDIT..8/8/2020<br />Revisited during storm. Still adore it. First read when I was like eight or nine. <br /><br />Gave it to my dad during the storm when I was done. He'd never read it. He finished it in a night and LOVED it. And no, did not guess the culprit.<br /><br />My review:<br /><br />Why is does this book not have a solid 5 star average rating? Oh no..my bias is showing.<br /><br />I first read this book as a child, after seeing my lovely Mamacita's copy. Through the years I revisit. Never loses its power.<br /><br />Agatha Christie's "Death comes as the end" is the only one of her books that I feature on my "favorite books of all time list". It differs from many of her books in several ways.<br /><br />First off..there is nothing..I repeat..nothing..cozy about this book. I first read it as a child and do not mind admitting it scared the heck out of me. Many of Christie's books have a cozy element to them. This does not.<br /><br />Second this book is just as much Historical Fiction as a mystery. It takes place in Ancient Egypt. I grew up obsessed with books about Egypt and this one doesn't disappoint. Historical fiction buffs..you will be transported to Egypt via this book. The atmosphere and setting are top notch.<br /><br />This book has some of the standard things..a murder..who did it..another murder. <br /><br />But this book is as much about the human element as the crime element..who we are, how we become the people we are, how does the world see us and is that view accurate? <br /><br />How will we grow and leave the past behind? I would so recommend Death comes as the end. It is interesting that I have read many an Agatha Christie book and while I liked some of them, none really got me involved as this book did. <br /><br />It is complex, deeply engaging both as Historical Fiction and as a mystery. Do not underestimate the deeply moving and Spiritual element to the story.<br /><br />A definite five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8463948796048346036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2701698430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5089941203738168913">This is the only Agatha Christie novel set in antiquity. The setting for this murder mystery novel is ancient Egypt. It is the most haunting of all her works because of the sheer number of people who get killed under mysterious circumstances. Seven people are killed before the murderer is caught. As always the climax is brilliant. Even though as a Christie fan, you would have guessed the murderer yet in the end you are left wondering at the brilliance of the plot. Great read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7855026912595741224" style="display:none">Choose Your Own Adventure!<br /><br />You are Imhotep, ka-priest of Ancient Egypt, ruler over a family of nitwits and schemers and busybodies, with drama enough to drive you insane. Poor fellow, all you want is a little peace... the kind of peace that is found in the arms of a gorgeous concubine. Who can blame you? The only sympathetic person in your life is your daughter, a lovely and tragic young widow. But sadly, the concubine turns out to be as big a drama queen as everyone else in your life and very bad things begin to happen. Bad things begin to happen to everyone! If this wasn’t bloodthirsty Ancient Egypt, the sheer body count that you have to deal with during this drawn-out massacre would definitely raise an eyebrow. Sometimes enough is enough! Whatever is a ka-priest to do?<br /><br />If you decide to further indulge your need for beautiful and powerful women, choose <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134216194">http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/...</a><br /><br />If you decide that life holds no more mystery for you and it is time to end it all, choose <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134197856">http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/...</a><br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2879203811?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken" href="/user/show/38999260-ken">Ken</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008196325" href="/book/show/35068926-death-comes-as-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2879203811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10159982925791288380">A unique entry in this Christie cannon sees the queen of crime tackle a suggestion by family friend Stephen Glanville tinder a mystery in the past.<br/>Deciding to take up his request, Christie opted to set this novel in Egypt 2000 BC.<br/><br/>Wisely choosing to have a family based drama as the main plot, it was easy to be transported to this era.<br/>With the father of the family bring home a concubine that unmuffles the other members of the household, it’s not long until she is found dead.<br/><br/>There’s a vast array of</span>
  <span id="freeText10159982925791288380" style="display:none">A unique entry in this Christie cannon sees the queen of crime tackle a suggestion by family friend Stephen Glanville tinder a mystery in the past.<br />Deciding to take up his request, Christie opted to set this novel in Egypt 2000 BC.<br /><br />Wisely choosing to have a family based drama as the main plot, it was easy to be transported to this era.<br />With the father of the family bring home a concubine that unmuffles the other members of the household, it’s not long until she is found dead.<br /><br />There’s a vast array of characters that can get confusing, but this does lead to a higher death count!<br />The plot was simple enough and as you start to suspect the next person, they are subsequently murdered.<br /><br />I liked the idea behind the novel rather than the story itself, it was an interesting and unique experiment.<br />This is best suited for those that wish to read ever Christie book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10159982925791288380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Although a murder mystery, there is a ton of family drama and entertaining relationship dynamics to follow. I highlighted many quotes from Ms. Christie's fabulous writing, but as a mystery, this is far from a favorite for me. However, I enjoyed it overall and would recommend it to any <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie' title='Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie</a> fan.<br/><br/><b>My favorite quote:</b><br/><i>"Not so easy to kill an old woman.       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pranta Ghosh Dastider" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pranta Ghosh Dastider" href="/user/show/20310470-pranta-ghosh-dastider">Pranta Ghosh Dastider</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711837357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8675886410395993288">What a story!! What a story indeed!!!<br/><br/>I admit, I have read very few of Christie stories, and only two of them weren't translated including this one. Here and now I am mesmerized by her fabulous storytelling. So organized well masked plot and witty characters! There were motive for many and killings took place, but why you may never be sure until the end. I had particularly two in my mind, and one of them turned out to be villainous. So, there is hint if you can observe well enough, but I admit, i</span>
  <span id="freeText8675886410395993288" style="display:none">What a story!! What a story indeed!!!<br /><br />I admit, I have read very few of Christie stories, and only two of them weren't translated including this one. Here and now I am mesmerized by her fabulous storytelling. So organized well masked plot and witty characters! There were motive for many and killings took place, but why you may never be sure until the end. I had particularly two in my mind, and one of them turned out to be villainous. So, there is hint if you can observe well enough, but I admit, it could have gone either way.<br /><br />All in all, my respect for the queen of mystery has increased greatly after reading. No doubt its one of her finest stories. Do read it everyone. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronique" href="/user/show/12371602-veronique">Veronique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007282395" href="/book/show/13551773-death-comes-as-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=r2019">r2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=stars-4-0">stars-4-0</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=c20th">c20th</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1667476067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2683461065159649377"><i>“Fear is incomplete knowledge”</i><br/><br/>Out of Christie’s huge writing output, <i>Death Comes As The End</i> is the only novel set in Ancient Egypt. While it still features murders, and quite a few of them (!), the description of life by the Nile, in all its intricacies, takes on the role of another character, and I’d even say the main one. <br/><br/>Archeology fascinated her, even before meeting Sir Max Mallowan (who became her second husband), and took a huge part of her life when she came to share his work and passion,</span>
  <span id="freeText2683461065159649377" style="display:none"><i>“Fear is incomplete knowledge”</i><br /><br />Out of Christie’s huge writing output, <i>Death Comes As The End</i> is the only novel set in Ancient Egypt. While it still features murders, and quite a few of them (!), the description of life by the Nile, in all its intricacies, takes on the role of another character, and I’d even say the main one. <br /><br />Archeology fascinated her, even before meeting Sir Max Mallowan (who became her second husband), and took a huge part of her life when she came to share his work and passion, spending months in excavation sites from Iraq to Syria. Much of her acquired knowledge was used in many of her more popular titles, such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16360.Murder_in_Mesopotamia__Hercule_Poirot___14_" title="Murder in Mesopotamia (Hercule Poirot, #14) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Murder in Mesopotamia</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6251565.Death_on_the_Nile__Hercule_Poirot___17_" title="Death on the Nile (Hercule Poirot, #17) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Death on the Nile</a>.<br /><br />Having the same interest as her (although nowhere near the same amount of knowledge), I really enjoyed this story. The mix of portrayal of life thousands of years ago with a murder mystery worked really well! Having said this, I wonder if other readers will feel the same. Christie after all is known for her depiction of the early and mid 20th century, with her sharp gaze on that society, that it might be too wide a change? Still, I loved it :O) I’m even more resolved to find time to read her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25394432.Come__Tell_Me_How_You_Live_Memories_from_archaeological_expeditions_in_the_mysterious_Middle_East" title="Come, Tell Me How You Live Memories from archaeological expeditions in the mysterious Middle East by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Come, Tell Me How You Live: Memories from archaeological expeditions in the mysterious Middle East</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2683461065159649377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1980221537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15866401751583684130"><i>“All life is a jest, Imhotep - and it is death who laughs last. Do you not hear it at every feast? Eat, drink and be merry, for tomorrow you die.”<br/></i><br/>Death Comes as the End is Dame Agatha's only historical mystery and she makes full use of her in-depth knowledge of Ancient Egypt. The detail of Egyptian artifacts and religious beliefs Dame Agatha weaved into this was delightful and made up for the odd dalliances with annoying love triangles. What it didn't quite achieve was to give some authenticity </span>
  <span id="freeText15866401751583684130" style="display:none"><i>“All life is a jest, Imhotep - and it is death who laughs last. Do you not hear it at every feast? Eat, drink and be merry, for tomorrow you die.”<br /></i><br />Death Comes as the End is Dame Agatha's only historical mystery and she makes full use of her in-depth knowledge of Ancient Egypt. The detail of Egyptian artifacts and religious beliefs Dame Agatha weaved into this was delightful and made up for the odd dalliances with annoying love triangles. What it didn't quite achieve was to give some authenticity to the characters which still seemed as if they had been copied out of an English country house setting. <br /> <br />I guess, in a way one could argue that the relationships between Christie's characters and their issues are universal, but I could not help imagine some of the characters having a strong London accent. <br /> <br />Never mind, it was a fun read.</span>

  <span id="freeText1264956646025132552" style="display:none">Oh! Once again, murder is easy. When you kill once, the next time will be much much easier, and the next, and the next..<br />I sort of felt like this wrote George R. R. Martin, ha!<br />This family at first appeared like others, women fighting for trivial stuff, men proving themselves amongst each other.. But, all of this was just a shallow picture, and Agatha succeded to prove how, deep down people often carry very different emotions than the ones they 'show to the world'.<br /><br />While I was coming to the end of this book, I could perfectly hear Poirot's voice saying: 'No doubt, you will evolve the most preposterous theories', and originally, I thought that murderer could be (among others, because, honestly I suspected almost everyone, well not Imhotep and servants) - Renisenb. And, I even suspected this old, crazy, wise Esa. Foolish me!<br />So, when two brothers were poisoned, and the moment when Yahmose survived, oh I started to believe that he indeed knew that the wine he drank with his brother was poisoned. Yes, the world is full of people like Yahmose, sadly.<br /><br />This book also tells a very romantic story between the Renisenb and Kameni and how beautiful is to 'choose something wonderful rather than something real'. </span>

<div id="review_1512174238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1512174238" />
    <a title="Sophie Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30243244-sophie-hannah"><img alt="Sophie Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593689330p2/30243244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1512174238?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie Hannah" href="/user/show/30243244-sophie-hannah">Sophie Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1512174238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7539333833043107263">Beautifully written. One of Agatha's very best standalones, and I would have given it five stars if it weren't for the fact that I guessed the murderer about halfway through. Still, that's probably my fault. The novel is elegant, perfectly structured, full of clues and misdirection, with a great cast of characters and possibly the most vile of all Agatha's horrid characters. A very satisfying read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8784025814471043174">This was surprising enjoyable. The story has a large cast, and it took me a while to get my head around all the characters. Then, Christie blew everything up with the introduction of concubine Nophret. Christie built the tension well as people begin dying. There's an amazingly high death count in this story, but I found the story held my interest right to the end. (I did figure out who the baddie was, but still liked this mystery.)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1507369353" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1507369353" />
    <a title="Jaksen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7233842-jaksen"><img alt="Jaksen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455934399p2/7233842.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1507369353?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaksen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaksen" href="/user/show/7233842-jaksen">Jaksen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507369353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10106544919706999470">An Agatha Christie I hadn't read! (I listened to this one, actually.)<br/><br/>I've been doing a lot of sewing - yeah, I'm old, female and retreating into something I did endlessly while in college - and so I like to listen to an occasional book while I'm working. I chose this one thinking it was probably a Miss Marple or Hercule Poirot. Boy was I wrong! This is a murder mystery set in ancient Egypt and you could learn a lot about the social mores and family structure of the times just by reading this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText10106544919706999470" style="display:none">An Agatha Christie I hadn't read! (I listened to this one, actually.)<br /><br />I've been doing a lot of sewing - yeah, I'm old, female and retreating into something I did endlessly while in college - and so I like to listen to an occasional book while I'm working. I chose this one thinking it was probably a Miss Marple or Hercule Poirot. Boy was I wrong! This is a murder mystery set in ancient Egypt and you could learn a lot about the social mores and family structure of the times just by reading this book. (Christie was an expert in this area, along with knowing her poisons.)<br /><br />The prominent members of an Egyptian family are starting to drop like flies, and you know how much salt brine, embalming oils and linen wrappings cost! (They talk about these things.) Suffice to say there is no official police or authorities to call in; the family has to sort of wing it and figure it out on their own. The thought that a family member or member of the household staff -servants or slaves - might be the murderer? Horrifying! Outrageous! But as the family maunders around and prays to their various gods and blames 'evil spirits,' - the first to go is the upper middle-aged patriarch's new concubine - the reader gets a glimpse of family hierarchies, the significance of being a female in this society, the role of servants and slaves, how marriages are arranged, and treatment of the elderly and children. It's a fascinating read, or listen, though my credulity was strained when other family members are done in - falling off a cliff, poisoned, drowned - one after another - and yet life just goes on. Tending to the barley fields. Preparing the flax. Washing the linen. Lathering one's body in oils and unguents. (I love that word, unguent.) <br /><br />I did not figure out who did what until the very end, and my main suspect who I was so sure had done it, turned out to be totally innocent. A great mystery set in an unlikely setting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10106544919706999470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=she-says">she-says</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer769452724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12802024290228941871">This book is excellent! It takes place in Ancient Egypt, and it is a murder mystery...of course. I love it! Christie makes sure that anyone could have done it...and you suspect everyone at different times. I adore how she develops her characters. Her main character, a woman named Renisenb, I found childish, ditzy, and even idiotic at times. Also, the book takes place during a time when women are not given much respect. The ending definitely surprised me! I would highly recommend this book. </span>

          </span>

We travel with Agatha Christie to ancient Egypt and find people no different in the historic past than today - some intelligent and some not, and there are those with petty jealousies, superstitions, imagined rivalries and, possibly, a murderous disposition.   <span id="freeText17657342148035658972" style="display:none">4 Stars. We travel with Agatha Christie to ancient Egypt and find people no different in the historic past than today - some intelligent and some not, and there are those with petty jealousies, superstitions, imagined rivalries and, possibly, a murderous disposition. Of course, this is a Christie novel! You are sure to enjoy the feeling of authenticity she brings to the rhythm of daily life for the Imhotep family living on the shores of the Nile near Thebes. Imhotep is a wealthy farmer and priest; his wife passed away years earlier, and he decides to take a concubine as life slowly winds down - someone young and sexy to make him smile. He even thinks it wise to leave Nofret with his three sons, Yahmose, Sobek, Ipy, and Renisenb his daughter, and their families, when he returns to the capital. Fatal mistake - the animosity quotient rises exponentially. When Nofret dies, family members suggest that it was Imhotep's wife from the great beyond expressing her displeasure at his actions. We follow the danger through the eyes of Renisenb, herself a young widow. Does Esa, Imhotep's elderly but wise mother, know the truth? (June 2020)</span>

<div id="review_380361036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380361036" />
    <a title="Candiss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2867198-candiss"><img alt="Candiss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325299894p2/2867198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380361036?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candiss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candiss" href="/user/show/2867198-candiss">Candiss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671543198" href="/book/show/3907362-death-comes-as-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2867198-candiss?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2867198-candiss?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2867198-candiss?shelf=mystery-thriller-suspense-crime">mystery-thriller-suspense-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380361036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3065452239301277679">Agatha Christie's <i>Death Comes as the End</i> is a good old-fashioned whodunnit with many layers of characterization and psychological intrigue. <br/><br/>Unlike Christie's many other mysteries, such as her beloved Hercule Poirot and Miss Marple series, this one takes place in ancient Egypt. Although the story is technically about the murder of a concubine, it's actually more about the family drama among and the psychological landscape of the central family's members. A ka-priest (priest whose job it is to ten</span>
  <span id="freeText3065452239301277679" style="display:none">Agatha Christie's <i>Death Comes as the End</i> is a good old-fashioned whodunnit with many layers of characterization and psychological intrigue. <br /><br />Unlike Christie's many other mysteries, such as her beloved Hercule Poirot and Miss Marple series, this one takes place in ancient Egypt. Although the story is technically about the murder of a concubine, it's actually more about the family drama among and the psychological landscape of the central family's members. A ka-priest (priest whose job it is to tend the family tomb of one or more individuals, and in return he inherits their estate) who has been widowed for many years falls for a concubine while traveling to another land, bringing her home with him. His family all have tangled webs of drama prior to the arrival of this newcomer - things dealing with inheritance, status, jockeying for position, as well as secret hatreds and jealousies and other personal issues - and the concubine is not a nice girl. She's young and beautiful, but she's manipulative, greedy, cruel, hateful of children, and deeply intelligent. She purposefully causes much strife, and eventually she is found dead. Fingers are pointed, mysteries are untangled, and all sorts of intrigue ensues. Then several other family members start turning up dead, one by one...<br /><br />I loved the setting. I am very keen on ancient Egyptian history, and Christie, while definitely being inventive to support her fiction, did some good research for this story. It felt authentic and believable. I wish she had written more historical setting mysteries! I also enjoyed the focus on the psychological aspects of the family's interactions and the fact that there was no detective/sleuth in this. The mystery was sussed out by family members who themselves were suspects the entire time.<br /><br />My only complaint: I thought the ending was a bit convenient and didn't fit perfectly with the rest of the story. The ultimate culprit seemed in the final few pages to be practically a different person than they were in the previous couple of hundred. I found it hard to believe they had done it. Christie did not make me believe their motivation. (This did not detract from the overall story, to be honest. I would take off a half-star, perhaps.)<br /><br />If you like mysteries or historical fiction or psychological/family drama, you should give this a try. It's a brisk read that kept me turning pages, and Christie is so good at fleshing out her characters on many levels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3065452239301277679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2760007296" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2760007296" />
    <a title="Kinan Diraneyya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8888352-kinan-diraneyya"><img alt="Kinan Diraneyya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518280921p2/8888352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2760007296?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kinan Diraneyya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kinan Diraneyya" href="/user/show/8888352-kinan-diraneyya">Kinan Diraneyya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8888352-kinan-diraneyya?shelf=novels-and-stories">novels-and-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2760007296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11533075332959921541">Death Comes as the End is the first novel that I have read for Agatha Christie although my father was the official publisher for her novels in the Middle East for so many years. I am not into crime stories, but I appreciate well-written people and social interactions and those are things that people often compliment in Agatha's novels.<br/><br/>So Agatha is most known for her crime novels; ironically, I was really enjoying the story until the crime occurred. People are indeed well-written, it is fascinati</span>
  <span id="freeText11533075332959921541" style="display:none">Death Comes as the End is the first novel that I have read for Agatha Christie although my father was the official publisher for her novels in the Middle East for so many years. I am not into crime stories, but I appreciate well-written people and social interactions and those are things that people often compliment in Agatha's novels.<br /><br />So Agatha is most known for her crime novels; ironically, I was really enjoying the story until the crime occurred. People are indeed well-written, it is fascinating how most of them relate to people that I know in real life and the way they deal with each other is just how I would have imagined it to be. Then someone dies and suddenly half of the characters lose their personality. Agatha controls her characters in the least realistic ways in order to fuel the murder mystery, which is very disappointing after what I saw in the first quarter of this book.<br /><br />There is a scene where three characters meet in secret to discuss their suspect list, this is one example of those "theatrical", unrealistic scenes that serve a certain purpose intended by the writer. These three characters go by all of the characters in the book including themselves, giving the reader different reasons to suspect each and every one of them, again, fueling the mystery in a way I consider cheap.<br /><br />Regarding the crime itself, I was expecting Detective Conan for grown-ups, but I ended up with Detective Conan as is. How a normal human can suddenly turn into a serial killer for the stupidest reasons and how he/she suddenly acquires the knowledge to craft all kinds of poisons and the acting abilities of Tom Hanks to cover it up. I might have said that I am not in it for the crime; however, the crime intervened with the social aspect and ruined most of it.<br /><br />Agatha attempts giving you the illusion that she delivered clues to the real killer through the entire story, which is exactly what makes a good crime novel in my opinion, but it is only an illusion. What she actually did was keeping enough reasons for everyone in the house to be the real killer and under that situation, it just didn't matter who he/she ended up being because it could have basically been anyone.<br /><br />On the bright side, characters that retained their personalities were enjoyable until the end. I am definitely willing to read more of Agatha Christie's novels based on that alone, although I have lower expectations now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11533075332959921541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_115415117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Meave" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/537203-meave"><img alt="Meave" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455989813p2/537203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115415117?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meave" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meave" href="/user/show/537203-meave">Meave</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115415117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10882196588103036776">Very odd. It's good when an author tries to stretch, you know, but it was still the same story, and I didn't like that inching-toward-monotheism business one bit; it seemed terribly disrespectful. Still, I guess all her stories are the same story, so to criticize this one in particular isn't fair; it was how the tone felt like a mixture of genuine narrative and this unpleasant "writing about savages" superiority. If she was taking it seriously, then it's too bad she was such a prejudiced old thi</span>
  <span id="freeText10882196588103036776" style="display:none">Very odd. It's good when an author tries to stretch, you know, but it was still the same story, and I didn't like that inching-toward-monotheism business one bit; it seemed terribly disrespectful. Still, I guess all her stories are the same story, so to criticize this one in particular isn't fair; it was how the tone felt like a mixture of genuine narrative and this unpleasant "writing about savages" superiority. If she was taking it seriously, then it's too bad she was such a prejudiced old thing; if she wasn't, then for shame, publishing a novel in which you are so disrespectful toward all your characters.<br /><br />The schizophrenia was too much. It could've been better, but old Aggie kept slipping into, like, "native talk" or whatever, which was gross. When she treated her ancient Egyptians like present-day British citizens, then the book was of a quality as the rest of her oeuvre. OH WELL; can't say I'm surprised.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10882196588103036776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1366575285" />
    <a title="Selah Pike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30034777-selah-pike"><img alt="Selah Pike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546303684p2/30034777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1366575285?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Selah Pike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Selah Pike" href="/user/show/30034777-selah-pike">Selah Pike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062074133" href="/book/show/12034506-death-comes-as-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30034777-selah-pike?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30034777-selah-pike?shelf=2020-owned-rereads">2020-owned-rereads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1366575285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9907940636586958673">I love the historical setting - it's so different for Christie. The plot, however, is vintage Christie. I actually figured out whodunnit at the halfway point, and then doubted myself because of *all* the red herrings. The love triangle, like all of Christie's love triangles, is annoying. I guess it's a reflection of her own troubled love life.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006138877" href="/book/show/8666442-death-comes-as-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6237864-nandakishore-varma?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213203720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9381446407773325205">Dame Agatha combines her expertise in writing mysteries with her not inconsiderable experience in archaeology - and what we get is a tale of murder set in ancient Egypt. As whodunits go, it's only so-so, but the background is fascinating.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2251966096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2251966096" />
    <a title="DeAnna Knippling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3166570-deanna-knippling"><img alt="DeAnna Knippling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442526565p2/3166570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2251966096?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DeAnna Knippling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DeAnna Knippling" href="/user/show/3166570-deanna-knippling">DeAnna Knippling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3166570-deanna-knippling?shelf=top-100-crime-novels-cwa">top-100-crime-novels-cwa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251966096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17882398849653151255">In ancient Egypt, a small family drama turns into tragedy when a new concubine is brought to the home of a wealthy priest. The body count mounts as the true nature of the family circle is revealed.<br/><br/>I picked this one up because it's on a best-of-all-time list of mysteries; I called the ending early, which generally disappoints me. It didn't here for some reason. The tension if you know what's coming is about the same as if you didn't, I think, because the danger seems worse if you know than if you</span>
  <span id="freeText17882398849653151255" style="display:none">In ancient Egypt, a small family drama turns into tragedy when a new concubine is brought to the home of a wealthy priest. The body count mounts as the true nature of the family circle is revealed.<br /><br />I picked this one up because it's on a best-of-all-time list of mysteries; I called the ending early, which generally disappoints me. It didn't here for some reason. The tension if you know what's coming is about the same as if you didn't, I think, because the danger seems worse if you know than if you don't. <br /><br />A lot of times with Agatha Christie, your head is spinning so fast that it's impossible to keep up. It's like...here she had mercy on her readers, to the extent that there's only about a short story's worth of standard Christie plot here. At a short novel length, it's easier to see what she's doing with clues and plot. If you want to see how a Christie mystery works, read this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17882398849653151255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/20754148-april-2021---death-comes-at-the-end">April 2021 - Death Comes at the End</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6prUX2SEEWJ4tMxrwTDYz8SngaR7UPfwMDCwjWff7KovVmUSkBQg42WWDCpBxVrj/EdjYw7SWWonU1YRuLcUag==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XAFRCUrfy1HvBzJiaOo5SnSE64RHJ4MS+jIdETqmGkiZzeBEvk/60PIl8iPoH7tmTGQJQzKlLYjtUfuN5c7iiA==')})
  }

Inspector Rudge begins to wonder just how many people have contributed to this extraordinary crime and whether he will ever unravel it. . .\n\nIn 1931 Agatha Christie, Dorothy L. Sayers, and 10 other crime writers from the newly formed Detection Club collaborated in publishing a unique crime novel. In a literary game of consequences, each author would write one chapter, leaving G.K. Chesterton to write a typically paradoxical prologue and Anthony Berkeley to tie up all the loose ends. In addition, all of the authors provided their own solutions in sealed envelopes, all of which appeared at the end of the book, with Agatha Christie\'s ingenious conclusion acknowledged at the time to be \'enough to make the book worth buying on its own\'. The authors of this novel are G.K. Chesterton, Canon Victor Whitechurch, G.D.H. Cole and Margaret Cole, Henry Wade, Agatha Christie, John Rhode, Milward Kennedy, Dorothy L. And what was going to happen to her impressionable young daughter?\n\nAnn Prentice is in love with Richard Cauldfield and hopes for new happiness. Her only daughter, cannot contemplate the idea of her mother marrying again and wrecks any chance of her remarriage.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie">About Agatha Christie</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1589991473p3/123715.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie">Agatha Christie
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
42,811
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9038013019833229834"><i>Agatha Christie also wrote romance novels under the pseudonym <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16273767.Mary_Westmacott' title='Mary Westmacott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary Westmacott</a></b>, and was occasionally published under the name <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19960421.Agatha_Christie_Mallowan' title='Agatha Christie Mallowan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie Mallowan</a></b>.</i><br/><br/>Agatha Christie is the best-selling author of all time. She wrote 66 crime novels and story collections, fourteen plays, and six novels under a pseudonym in Romance. Her books have sold over a billion copies in the English language and a billion in t</span>
  <span id="freeText9038013019833229834" style="display:none"><i>Agatha Christie also wrote romance novels under the pseudonym <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16273767.Mary_Westmacott" title="Mary Westmacott" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Westmacott</a></b>, and was occasionally published under the name <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19960421.Agatha_Christie_Mallowan" title="Agatha Christie Mallowan" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie Mallowan</a></b>.</i><br /><br />Agatha Christie is the best-selling author of all time. She wrote 66 crime novels and story collections, fourteen plays, and six novels under a pseudonym in Romance. Her books have sold over a billion copies in the English language and a billion in translation. According to Index Translationum, she remains the most-translated individual author, having been translated into at least 103 languages. She is the creator of two of the most enduring figures in crime literature-Hercule Poirot and Miss Jane Marple-and author of <i>The Mousetrap</i>, the longest-running play in the history of modern theatre. <br /><br />Agatha Mary Clarissa Miller was born in Torquay, Devon, England, U.K., as the youngest of three. The Millers had two other children: Margaret Frary Miller (1879–1950), called Madge, who was eleven years Agatha's senior, and Louis Montant Miller (1880–1929), called Monty, ten years older than Agatha. <br /><br />Before marrying and starting a family in London, she had served in a Devon hospital during the First World War, tending to troops coming back from the trenches. During the First World War, she worked at a hospital as a nurse; later working at a hospital pharmacy, a job that influenced her work, as many of the murders in her books are carried out with poison. During the Second World War, she worked as a pharmacy assistant at University College Hospital, London, acquiring a good knowledge of poisons which feature in many of her novels.<br /><br />Her first novel, <i>The Mysterious Affair at Styles</i>, came out in 1920. During her first marriage, Agatha published six novels, a collection of short stories, and a number of short stories in magazines.<br /><br />In late 1926, Agatha's husband, Archie, revealed that he was in love with another woman, Nancy Neele, and wanted a divorce. On 8 December 1926 the couple quarreled, and Archie Christie left their house, Styles, in Sunningdale, Berkshire, to spend the weekend with his mistress at Godalming, Surrey. That same evening Agatha disappeared from her home, leaving behind a letter for her secretary saying that she was going to Yorkshire. Her disappearance caused an outcry from the public, many of whom were admirers of her novels. Despite a massive manhunt, she was not found for eleven days.<br /><br />In 1930, Christie married archaeologist Max Mallowan (Sir Max from 1968) after joining him in an archaeological dig. Their marriage was especially happy in the early years and remained so until Christie's death in 1976.<br /><br />Christie frequently used familiar settings for her stories. Christie's travels with Mallowan contributed background to several of her novels set in the Middle East. Other novels (such as <i>And Then There Were None</i>) were set in and around Torquay, where she was born. Christie's 1934 novel <i>Murder on the Orient Express</i> was written in the Hotel Pera Palace in Istanbul, Turkey, the southern terminus of the railway. The hotel maintains Christie's room as a memorial to the author. The Greenway Estate in Devon, acquired by the couple as a summer residence in 1938, is now in the care of the National Trust.<br /><br />Christie often stayed at Abney Hall in Cheshire, which was owned by her brother-in-law, James Watts. She based at least two of her stories on the hall: the short story <i>The Adventure of the Christmas Pudding</i>, and the novel <i>After the Funeral</i>. Abney Hall became Agatha's greatest inspiration for country-house life, with all the servants and grandeur which have been woven into her plots.<br /><br /><br />To honour her many literary works, she was appointed Commander of the Order of the British Empire in the 1956 New Year Honours. The next year, she became the President of the Detection Club. <br /><br /><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agatha_Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia entry for Agatha Christie</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9038013019833229834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
